  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2ca89968-5eaa-43fd-99b8-4a2f55fbbd53'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer2209094688539770917">One of the most popular and critically acclaimed comic book titles of all time, <i>New York Times</i> best-selling author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Neil Gaiman</a>'s masterpiece <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40372-the-sandman' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>The Sandman</i>
</a> set new standards for mature, lyrical fantasy and graphic narrative. Now, Vertigo and DC Comics are proud to present the third of four definitive Absolute Editions collecting this groundbreaking series in its entirety.</span>
  <span id="freeText2209094688539770917" style="display:none">One of the most popular and critically acclaimed comic book titles of all time, <i>New York Times</i> best-selling author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a>'s masterpiece <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40372-the-sandman" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Sandman</i>
</a> set new standards for mature, lyrical fantasy and graphic narrative. Now, Vertigo and DC Comics are proud to present the third of four definitive Absolute Editions collecting this groundbreaking series in its entirety. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Absolute Sandman, Volume Three</i>
</b> reprints issues 40-56 of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40372-the-sandman" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Sandman</i>
</a> and <i>The Sandman Special</i> 1 and features remastered coloring prepared especially for this edition on issues 40-49 and the Special. This volume also includes an introduction by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9931.Jill_Thompson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jill Thompson</a> (artist for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25105.The_Sandman_Vol_7" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Sandman, Vol 7: Brief Lives</i>
</a>), a never-before-reprinted story by Gaiman and artist <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10224.Michael_Zulli" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Zulli</a>, a complete reproduction of the one-shot <i>The Endless Gallery</i> as well as two additional 8-pages galleries, and the original script and thumbnail pencils by Gaiman and artist <a>P. Craig Russell</a> for the acclaimed story "Ramadan" from <i>The Sandman 50.</i></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=classics">classics</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186370342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12463710447042276245">I picked this up and started reading it the moment I finished volume 2. I hardly remember what was what anymore, and since it's all really one big story it hardly matters. I have read Sandman through at least four times (I've read individual storylines or even individual issues even more than that) and I will read it at least that many times again. It seems like I give the whole thing a re-read every three years or so. What can I say, it's pure magic.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_972457653" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/972457653" />
    <a title="Artemisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1165481-artemisa"><img alt="Artemisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246839165p2/1165481.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/972457653?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Artemisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Artemisa" href="/user/show/1165481-artemisa">Artemisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1165481-artemisa?shelf=mythology-fantasy">mythology-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1165481-artemisa?shelf=comics-or-graphic-novel">comics-or-graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1165481-artemisa?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer972457653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7269667847107737590">I didn't really care for the first arc in this book. It was nice too see a bit more of the endless, but the quest is so so. I like the Orpheus bit, but Desire is starting to give me the creeps...<br/>Then came the tavern at the end of the worlds arc. This is another multiple PoV arc, most of the stories only connect marginally with the endless, but I need an annotated sandman to get all the references in the stories, because I spotted enough of them to know there are many more I didn't get.<br/>This arc p</span>
  <span id="freeText7269667847107737590" style="display:none">I didn't really care for the first arc in this book. It was nice too see a bit more of the endless, but the quest is so so. I like the Orpheus bit, but Desire is starting to give me the creeps...<br />Then came the tavern at the end of the worlds arc. This is another multiple PoV arc, most of the stories only connect marginally with the endless, but I need an annotated sandman to get all the references in the stories, because I spotted enough of them to know there are many more I didn't get.<br />This arc plot goes: several travelers are caught in a storm, find refuge in a tavern, and tell stories, to pass the time and earn their keep.<br /><br />Between this 2 arcs there's this beautiful Arabian Nights style story called Ramadan. I believe it's issue 50. It is one of my favourite issues so far, along with the closing the gates of Hell issue. In the end there's the script and the behind the scenes, how this came to be, story.<br /><br />I switched to the Absolute version of Sandman because it does wonders for the art. And in this book there are some of the most beautiful pages I have seen.<br />In Ramadan there is this beautiful Arabian Nights style, full of merengue toped spires, and Arabian inspired lettering, and jewels and markets full of people and wonders.<br /><br />In the tavern arc, each story is drawn in a very different style, some of them I loved, they could almost tell the story with no words, some were more normal comics style, some were creepy, but they fitted the stories being told...<br /><br />And for all the Fables fans out there I'll just say this. Jack of Fables is a total Easter Egg. I'm not the recognised the artist type of girl, but I totally guessed who draw the art on the first arc. There is a character there that could be Jack's brother.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7269667847107737590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_43455709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/43455709" />
    <a title="Jack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1495381-jack"><img alt="Jack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1221504923p2/1495381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43455709?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack" href="/user/show/1495381-jack">Jack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43455709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14179400925868385697">This sat on my shelves for about 6 months before I read it. I was saving it for when I could really enjoy it, and I'm glad I did. The "Brief Lives" storyline is significantly longer and more personal than some of the more adventure-centric fun of earlier stories. "Brief Lives" is bookended by one-shot views of how dreams effect history, mythology and the way our stories are told and remembered. There are stories-within-stories, and the context only gets thicker after that. Interestingly, the tit</span>
  <span id="freeText14179400925868385697" style="display:none">This sat on my shelves for about 6 months before I read it. I was saving it for when I could really enjoy it, and I'm glad I did. The "Brief Lives" storyline is significantly longer and more personal than some of the more adventure-centric fun of earlier stories. "Brief Lives" is bookended by one-shot views of how dreams effect history, mythology and the way our stories are told and remembered. There are stories-within-stories, and the context only gets thicker after that. Interestingly, the titular characters plays only a tangential role in many of the stories, which gives this volume a less focussed air than the two preceeding. I had the feeling that Gaiman was enjoying the world he had created, but had more ideas in him than could be wrapped around the one character. The result is a series of diversions from the overarching "plot" that all share the same thrust. Interestingly, I was expecting a big payoff at the end of "Brief Lives" because it's the central narrative, but you really don't get it until the end of all the disjointed stories.<br /><br />Also, I'm not the first to be profoundly impressed by P. Craig Russel's treatment of Gaiman's "Ramadan" story for issue #50. I'm going to have to track down more of his work.<br /><br />Enthralling, through-and-through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14179400925868385697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1868392195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868392195" />
    <a title="Nigel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5020684-nigel"><img alt="Nigel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442514397p2/5020684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1868392195?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigel" href="/user/show/5020684-nigel">Nigel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5020684-nigel?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868392195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15262708168351473294">I started being diligent about reviewing the books I read here as a form of diary. I've never been vey good at diaries but I do like writing about books, and I tend to associate books with the times and places I read them. I regret that I was a bit slow about including graphic novels, but that's neither here not there. So I'm prefacing this review with a remark almost entirely of interest to none but myself. <br/><br/>The reason for the gap between the review of volume one in this series and the subsequen</span>
  <span id="freeText15262708168351473294" style="display:none">I started being diligent about reviewing the books I read here as a form of diary. I've never been vey good at diaries but I do like writing about books, and I tend to associate books with the times and places I read them. I regret that I was a bit slow about including graphic novels, but that's neither here not there. So I'm prefacing this review with a remark almost entirely of interest to none but myself. <br /><br />The reason for the gap between the review of volume one in this series and the subsequent volumes was because volume three and four arrived from the library weeks ago and volume two only arrived the other day. I'm not complaining, I'm amazed and delighted to have them, even of only on loan, and I'm delighted that they're out there in the system for others to enjoy. I was searching for a copy of Overture, actually, when I came across the Absolutes in the system and promptly decided that it was time to read the whole series. Volume five is there too, but, apparently, 'for library use only.' Since it consists of ancillary stories, and the main story ends in volume four, I'll get by without it for now. <br /><br />Anyway, yay libraries, as Lucien would no doubt agree.<br /><br />Onto Brief Lives, then, the longest story so far. Delirium decides it's time to find the lost brother of the Endless and ask him to come back. After some toing and froing, Dream, on the rebound from a break-up, goes along with her, half as a distraction, half in the hopes of running into hos lady-love, whoever she may be. Throughout the series it has become apparent that Dream is his own worst enemy or his own best friend, depending on how you view things. Certainly he is making decisions that lead to certain inescapable conclusions all the while insisting that he's doing them for other reasons and he hasn't really changed at all. Their search sets of events which damage and destroy certain lives, and this actually bothers him. In order to find his brother he has to make a certain sacrifice. Why does he do it? His sense of obligation and responsibility has broadened, perhaps, or he has become aware of blind spots and gaps in his approach to them, and maybe this is the breaking point. It's all there now, all ready to go. What's next is inevitable. <br /><br />After Brief Lives comes Worlds End, more masterful stories, including the great Wolfe homage and big sign saying SOMEONE IS GOING TO DIE which, in case you were slow on the uptake, is followed by a massive vision of a funeral. Artists include Mike Zulli, and there's another cruel but lush Zulli story right at the end. The script for Ramadan is included, and it's possibly the least informative of all the scripts, except to compare it to Russel's gorgeous execution of the story and the layouts is stunning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15262708168351473294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20768655-maggie-gordon?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20768655-maggie-gordon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20768655-maggie-gordon?shelf=favourite-author">favourite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20768655-maggie-gordon?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer626371041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8576238896481489583">The third volume of the Absolute Sandman collection contains several short stories and one overarching tale that has serious repercussions for poor Dream. <br/><br/>The anthology stories in this volume are quite diverse. There's the rather famous Ramadan story with the vibrant artwork that is so different from the usual tone of the series. There's a story that reminds us that Daniel still exists, and readers are introduced to World's End, the pub where people tell stories. There we hear about Cluracan aga</span>
  <span id="freeText8576238896481489583" style="display:none">The third volume of the Absolute Sandman collection contains several short stories and one overarching tale that has serious repercussions for poor Dream. <br /><br />The anthology stories in this volume are quite diverse. There's the rather famous Ramadan story with the vibrant artwork that is so different from the usual tone of the series. There's a story that reminds us that Daniel still exists, and readers are introduced to World's End, the pub where people tell stories. There we hear about Cluracan again (foreshadowing!), and about a girl who disguised herself as a boy to work on a sailing ship (readers get a glimpse at Hob and another immortal). There's a tale about Richard Prez, the best president the United States has ever seen, and, finally, a story about the necropolis (a place that becomes important next volume). All of these stories are fun and interesting on their own, but they each also contribute to the overall story that Gaiman is telling, and hint at a variety of things to come. <br /><br />The most important stories are The Song of Orpheus and Brief Lives. The Song of Orpheus shows readers how Dream's son ended up as an undying head. It's tragic and provides a rather sharp window into Dream's personality. In Brief Lives, a multi-issue narrative, Delirium decides that she must find their lost brother Destruction. Every sibling she goes to refuses to help her, but Dream agrees as he struggling to get over a lover and hopes that he might see her in the mortal realm again. The two go on a rather destructive hunt for their brother's former friends, though all of them seem to die just before the two Endless can find them. In the end, Dream enters into a bargain that he does not want to in order to find Destruction. He agrees to release his son. Meeting Destruction is quite a hoot. He's trying so hard to capture his creative side after leaving his mantle. He tries to counsel Dream to do the same, but Dream's path is stubbornly set. Destruction leaves Earth, asking his strange, talking dog to watch over his sister. <br /><br />It's only after reading the last few volumes of the Sandman that one recognises the true significance of these stories. Dream has reached the limits of how much he can change. He's tired, frustrated, but still so bound to duty. This volume is the perfect set up to the end of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8576238896481489583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_451926277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451926277" />
    <a title="Shannon Appelcline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10160415-shannon-appelcline"><img alt="Shannon Appelcline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339479517p2/10160415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/451926277?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon Appelcline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon Appelcline" href="/user/show/10160415-shannon-appelcline">Shannon Appelcline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10160415-shannon-appelcline?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10160415-shannon-appelcline?shelf=comics-dc">comics-dc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10160415-shannon-appelcline?shelf=comics-fantasy">comics-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451926277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18328801363974235051">I didn’t expect a lot from the little ten-page “Fear of Falling”, but I forget how good Gaiman is with shorts. This has great characters and a terrific punchline [9/10]. “The Parliament of Rooks” offers a nice look at the background of Eve, Cain, and Abel. When I first read it, it might have seemed more important than it does now [7/10]. “Orpheus” is a bit more straightforward than many of the other Sandman stories, probably because it was created as the foundation of the entire back-half of the</span>
  <span id="freeText18328801363974235051" style="display:none">I didn’t expect a lot from the little ten-page “Fear of Falling”, but I forget how good Gaiman is with shorts. This has great characters and a terrific punchline [9/10]. “The Parliament of Rooks” offers a nice look at the background of Eve, Cain, and Abel. When I first read it, it might have seemed more important than it does now [7/10]. “Orpheus” is a bit more straightforward than many of the other Sandman stories, probably because it was created as the foundation of the entire back-half of the series. Still, it has its minutes of shock and grief that raise the story up, and when it was came out, the first look at the missing Endless was probably pretty exciting [8/10]. “Brief Lives” is the picture-perfect center to Sandman. It cleans up the plotlines hinted at throughout the first half of the series and sets in motion everything that follows. The interactions of Dream and Delirium in the real world are also some of the funniest parts of the whole series [10/10]. “Ramadan” is the most fairy tale like of the Sandman stories and beautifully drawn [8/10]. “World’s End” is an interesting new take on a short story collection. The frame itself is actually quite intriguing, both in the story of our two modern people and in the Reality Storm they see. The stories themselves vary. Some are just OK, but “Hob’s Leviathan” is very good and the Prez story is entirely brilliant [8.5/10]. As usal, the stuff that closes out the volume is nice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18328801363974235051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2323293160" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2323293160" />
    <a title="CC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2348515-cc"><img alt="CC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520722720p2/2348515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2323293160?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CC" href="/user/show/2348515-cc">CC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2323293160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1279800919734239012">I have owned The Sandman in almost every iteration, from the original monthly comic books to softbound 'graphic novel' collected works. With Absolute Sandman, I will never need another copy as they are simply beautiful. Each large leather bound tome is encased in a matching sleeve with artwork by the legendary Dave McKean. His distinctive stylings are further reproduced on each cover, with attractive stamped detail and silver lettering. Whether you are an old fan or a newcomer, I can't recommend</span>
  <span id="freeText1279800919734239012" style="display:none">I have owned The Sandman in almost every iteration, from the original monthly comic books to softbound 'graphic novel' collected works. With Absolute Sandman, I will never need another copy as they are simply beautiful. Each large leather bound tome is encased in a matching sleeve with artwork by the legendary Dave McKean. His distinctive stylings are further reproduced on each cover, with attractive stamped detail and silver lettering. Whether you are an old fan or a newcomer, I can't recommend this set of books highly enough. They are still as fresh and immersive today as the first time I found them, and stand up well as the pinnacle of the author's storytelling powers. I'll forever be appreciative of Neil Gaiman's other work but for me The Sandman is a true legacy.<br /><br />Volume Three begins with a foreword from the artist who illustrated "Brief Lives", Jill Thompson. Brief Lives is a standout story for me because we get to follow Delirium of the Endless in her search for her brother, Destruction, and learn more about this elusive character. It is in this set of stories that the true nature of the Sandman finally begins to reveal itself, and seeds are sown for the tragedies to come. There are also many one-shot stories at the end of this volume that are highly enjoyable, such as Cluracan's Tale and World's End. For myself, the jewel in this particular book comes in the form of a story called Ramadan, which was written by Neil Gaiman for the landmark issue number 50. Illustrated by P. Craig Russell, Ramadan tells the tale of Haroun Al Raschid, King of Baghdad, whose only wish is to preserve the beauty of his city. Of all the Sandman stories, I find Ramadan to be one of the most affecting, a powerful piece of visual art.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1279800919734239012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3159462900" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3159462900" />
    <a title="Óscar López" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45786552-scar-l-pez"><img alt="Óscar López" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443983049p2/45786552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3159462900?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Óscar López" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Óscar López" href="/user/show/45786552-scar-l-pez">Óscar López</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3159462900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15411934649193652555">This is the third volume in the beautiful Absolute edition of Sandman. It collects issues 40-56, plus a couple of short stories and the usual miscellany of artwork and merchandise. It covers the "Brief Lives" storyline and the "World's End" series of interconnected short stories.<br/><br/>"Brief Lives" recounts the search for Destruction, the missing Endless. Delirium, the manic pixie dream girl of the Endless teams up with Morpheus to go looking for their estranged brother, meeting some memorable charact</span>
  <span id="freeText15411934649193652555" style="display:none">This is the third volume in the beautiful Absolute edition of Sandman. It collects issues 40-56, plus a couple of short stories and the usual miscellany of artwork and merchandise. It covers the "Brief Lives" storyline and the "World's End" series of interconnected short stories.<br /><br />"Brief Lives" recounts the search for Destruction, the missing Endless. Delirium, the manic pixie dream girl of the Endless teams up with Morpheus to go looking for their estranged brother, meeting some memorable characters along the way and a mysterious opposing force. I fell in love with Delirium; she's sweet, adorable and clueless beyond any reality.<br /><br />"World's End" makes wonderful use of the story-within-a-story plot device, as a group of travelers of different planes of existence wait for the passing of a reality storm, and begin sharing unique tales - rich, imaginative and fantastic. The final story ends in a tremendously sad foreshadowing of the things to come, as The Sandman is nearing its end.<br /><br />Two of the other short stories are worth mentioning: "The Song of Orpheus" narrates the fate of Morpheus' son, and "Ramadan” – straight out of the Arabian Nights ... oh my goodness, this is one of the best stories ever to be presented in a graphic novel, an undisputed example of the power of this medium!<br /><br />I have only praise and admiration for Neil Gaiman, this is his masterpiece and the quintessential graphic novel, a world of imagination and unforgettable stories and characters, where anyone would love to get lost. I'm looking forward to the final volume, with the sadness of someone who visits a dear place for the last time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15411934649193652555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2166122698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2166122698" />
    <a title="Wade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50871538-wade"><img alt="Wade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451665112p2/50871538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2166122698?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wade" href="/user/show/50871538-wade">Wade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2166122698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10204732384159601611">In this volume, we spend the first half with Dream and his sister Delirium trying to find their missing brother, who does not wish to be found, and the second half in a sort of Arabian Nights styled collection of, loosely connected, (sometimes nested) short stories that serve to add fullness to this world Gaiman has created in The Sandman.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed the sections with Delirium, she adds much needed color to the series, and this section also highlights the gradual changes that have been taki</span>
  <span id="freeText10204732384159601611" style="display:none">In this volume, we spend the first half with Dream and his sister Delirium trying to find their missing brother, who does not wish to be found, and the second half in a sort of Arabian Nights styled collection of, loosely connected, (sometimes nested) short stories that serve to add fullness to this world Gaiman has created in The Sandman.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the sections with Delirium, she adds much needed color to the series, and this section also highlights the gradual changes that have been taking place in Dream, the Sandman himself, throughout the series, which is refreshing, especially given that he is in denial concerning the changes. Also in the section we finally meet that last member of The Endless, whom I've been curious about, and though his time in the page is too short, he is a joy to encounter.<br /><br />In the Arabian Nights-esque section, I especially enjoyed how he worked with different artists on the different stories to give each their own, unique feel.<br /><br />All throughout this series, and especially in the second half of this volume, it was fun to see some of the ideas budding that bloomed into some of Gaiman's later works like: American Gods, Neverwhere, Ocean at the End of the Lane, and Graveyard Book (there were probably others hinted at, but I either forgot or missed them).<br /><br />The end of this volume sort of threw me, and I have no idea what might be coming next, which gives me a greater-than-usual sense of the connectedness of the whole series, which is very good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10204732384159601611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2288610755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288610755" />
    <a title="Ramiz Qudsi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9858514-ramiz-qudsi"><img alt="Ramiz Qudsi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533716139p2/9858514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288610755?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramiz Qudsi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramiz Qudsi" href="/user/show/9858514-ramiz-qudsi">Ramiz Qudsi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9858514-ramiz-qudsi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288610755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12885879374371912177">Neil Gaiman continues to amaze me as he weave magic of words and impress upon how dreams are made up of real stuff.<br/>Book three is mostly about Dream, as in he is actually present in most of the stories and is not just in the background. Him and Delirium went on a journey and as you go along with them you get invested in it yourself. Chapters with Delirium in it were hilarious and exceptionally delightful, which might be a bit ironic, given that she use to be Delight and then change forced her to </span>
  <span id="freeText12885879374371912177" style="display:none">Neil Gaiman continues to amaze me as he weave magic of words and impress upon how dreams are made up of real stuff.<br />Book three is mostly about Dream, as in he is actually present in most of the stories and is not just in the background. Him and Delirium went on a journey and as you go along with them you get invested in it yourself. Chapters with Delirium in it were hilarious and exceptionally delightful, which might be a bit ironic, given that she use to be Delight and then change forced her to be Delirium. More than anything, it was the way those two endless interacted with the physical world which made it pure delight. And the Raven was just added to the comedy of situation. Destiny was of course as stoic as ever.<br />The chemistry between Delirium and Dream was worth every page they were in together. It is just amazing, even better than the one between Death and Dream. Death tend to big sister Dream often, and when you learn the kind of uuummmm...I don't know, person?, when you learn the kind of person that Dream is it makes perfect sense for Death to be so, which honestly is quite nice. With Delirium though, it is quite the opposite. Dream has to act as big and caring brother and after some initial hiccups he does prove to be a great brother!<br /><br />Overall, just another fantastic collection!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12885879374371912177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3639693580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3639693580" />
    <a title="Shane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2703259-shane"><img alt="Shane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1256174755p2/2703259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3639693580?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shane" href="/user/show/2703259-shane">Shane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3639693580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16731503205056334943">While it's undeniable that Mr. Gaiman began his comics career as a skilled writer (the first collected edition, <i>Preludes and Nocturnes</i> was justifiably a sensation thirty years ago), it is equally true that, like any artist, his genius evolved over time. By the time we get to this third volume of the Absolute Editions we are deep in the original 75-comic run, issues 40 to 56 from 1992-93 and he is at the peak of his skill. <i>The Worlds' End</i> arc (#51-56) is maybe my favorite in all the Sandman canon</span>
  <span id="freeText16731503205056334943" style="display:none">While it's undeniable that Mr. Gaiman began his comics career as a skilled writer (the first collected edition, <i>Preludes and Nocturnes</i> was justifiably a sensation thirty years ago), it is equally true that, like any artist, his genius evolved over time. By the time we get to this third volume of the Absolute Editions we are deep in the original 75-comic run, issues 40 to 56 from 1992-93 and he is at the peak of his skill. <i>The Worlds' End</i> arc (#51-56) is maybe my favorite in all the Sandman canon. Here we have a near-unparalleled storyteller telling fabulous stories. Maybe some of the strength here is that after so much past as prologue, His Royal Dreamness is a supporting character, as are his now-famous family. These are tales told by (more or less) normal people (or beings, or whatever), and they are <u>so well told</u>. <br /><br />If you already have the series in another format I recommend the Absolute editions for their incredible quality, especially if you are interested in the ephemera that is added - annotated scripts, alternate covers, previously unpublished artwork and the like. But I hope that is you, because these versions of these stories are truly wonderful.<br /><br />The content, unhesitatingly recommended, an absolute must for lovers of mythic stories so very well told. The edition, recommended for Sandman fans with the spending power to bring it home.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16731503205056334943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2829219525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2829219525" />
    <a title="Qas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5980286-qas"><img alt="Qas" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2829219525?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Qas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Qas" href="/user/show/5980286-qas">Qas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2829219525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1449607404132710844">Volume Three of The Absolute Sandman is the series returning to top form.<br/><br/>The first volume felt wondrous, epic, and heartfelt. The second for me wasn’t as consistent as the first, and lacked the punch I expected. However, all is back as it should be with the third. <br/><br/>It starts with a fantastic arc that brings together Death and Delirium in a poignant and satisfying way. Following on from this, we get a few single-issue shorts, including the standout Ramadan. The issue has a visual style miles apart</span>
  <span id="freeText1449607404132710844" style="display:none">Volume Three of The Absolute Sandman is the series returning to top form.<br /><br />The first volume felt wondrous, epic, and heartfelt. The second for me wasn’t as consistent as the first, and lacked the punch I expected. However, all is back as it should be with the third. <br /><br />It starts with a fantastic arc that brings together Death and Delirium in a poignant and satisfying way. Following on from this, we get a few single-issue shorts, including the standout Ramadan. The issue has a visual style miles apart from anything else in the series, but fits in perfectly in tone and style, making it exactly the right change of pace needed at that point.<br /><br />We then move on to another arc, made up of smaller stories that build to a whole, and this too is satisfying and consistently entertaining.<br /><br />Overall, this is a volume full of purely original and thoughtful stories.<br /><br />5 stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1449607404132710844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9639476657928066684">Every time I read Brief Lives I suddenly remember that it's possibly my favourite of the whole series. This is a stunning volume of work. Incredible storytelling. The way the art and the words merge together is perfect. The way this arc brings together threads laid down in earlier stories and twists, setting us up for what comes next. Just perfection. <br/>The other stories here are also good, and there are a couple of double page spreads that are just heart stoppingly beautiful. <br/>If you have been won</span>
  <span id="freeText9639476657928066684" style="display:none">Every time I read Brief Lives I suddenly remember that it's possibly my favourite of the whole series. This is a stunning volume of work. Incredible storytelling. The way the art and the words merge together is perfect. The way this arc brings together threads laid down in earlier stories and twists, setting us up for what comes next. Just perfection. <br />The other stories here are also good, and there are a couple of double page spreads that are just heart stoppingly beautiful. <br />If you have been wondering if the absolute versions are with your money, I think this volume cements that they are. Just gorgeous.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Jdvtkp6cNTyZalPHEku2AP3ryIhWXiCu4mXtYvfs8rH732Sfkm864LsWVNw5iNrnDDQWmt/aBW1pgcGQpjFuFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aRxt2hr38HwoI0z3ZKDJGWaTXGcz36XGX74vQETzGTy3GOTXFgT/oApfS+xPY6X+l0yCdbpbgAXUWgOyFS6FmA==')})
  }

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
